<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3942128061416194557">It was only a matter of time before Terry Pratchett would win the minds and hearts of America. Already a worldwide sensation and Great Britain's indisputable number one author, this intellectually audacious and effortlessly hilarious writer sold more hardcover books in the United Kingdom during the previous decade than any other living novelist. His novels have reigned sup</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3942128061416194557">It was only a matter of time before Terry Pratchett would win the minds and hearts of America. Already a worldwide sensation and Great Britain's indisputable number one author, this intellectually audacious and effortlessly hilarious writer sold more hardcover books in the United Kingdom during the previous decade than any other living novelist. His novels have reigned supreme on English bestseller lists since before the Iron Lady left Downing Street, and though some things have changed since then, Pratchett, thankfully, continues to pen insightfully irreverent tales set in a world a lot like our own -- only different.<br /><br />Celebrated as one of the keenest practitioners of satire and parody at work today -- alongside Kurt Vonnegut, Douglas Adams, and Carl Hiaasen -- Terry Pratchett commands a loyal and ever-increasing number of readers and appreciative critics from coast to coast in our own country. As he skewers all aspects of modern life -- and especially our sacred cows -- Pratchett makes us laugh and challenges us to think. And he's at his sharpest, most uproarious best in <em>Thief of Time.</em><br /><br />Everybody wants more time, which is why on Discworld its management is entrusted to the experts: the venerable Monks of History, who store it and pump it from where it's wasted, like underwater (after all, how much time does a codfish really need?) to places like cities, where harried citizens are forever lamenting, "Oh where does the time go?"<br /><br />And while everyone always talks about slowing down, one clever soul is about to stop. Stop time, that is. For good. Going against everything known (and the nine tenths of everything that remains unknown), a young horologist has been commissioned to build the world's first truly accurate clock. It falls to History Monk Lu-Tze and his apprentice Lobsang Ludd to find the timepiece and stop it before it starts. For if the Perfect Clock starts ticking, Time -- as we know it -- will stop. And then the trouble will really begin.<br /><br />A superb send-up of science and philosophy, religion and death (after all, isn't that where time stops, for most of us, anyway?), and a host of other timely topics, <em>Thief of Time</em> provides the perfect opportunity to kick back and unwind. So don't put off till tomorrow what you could do today. Read <em>Thief of Time.</em> Right this minute. Because tomorrow may not come. (You'll have to read the book to find out why. This is a Terry Pratchett novel, after all.)<br /><br /><em>Tick ...</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3942128061416194557">...more</a>

      </div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_6565863').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_6565863').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_6565863').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script></div>
</li>

<span id="freeTextContainer7413240761752554298">Well, I did not love Lu-Tze, or the History Monks, or the Glass Clock plot...BUT, this being a Pratchett book, it was easy to find plenty of other things to go gaga over.<br /><br />- This exchange between Susan and her grandfather:<br /><br /><em>"They're going to do something to time? I thought they weren't allowed to do things like that."<br /><br />NO. BUT HUMANS CAN. IT HAS BEEN DONE ONCE BEFORE.<br /><br />"No one would be that stu---"<br /><br />Susan stopped. Of course someone would be that stupid. Some humans would do anything to see if it was possi</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7413240761752554298">Well, I did not love Lu-Tze, or the History Monks, or the Glass Clock plot...BUT, this being a Pratchett book, it was easy to find plenty of other things to go gaga over.<br /><br />- This exchange between Susan and her grandfather:<br /><br /><em>"They're going to do something to time? I thought they weren't allowed to do things like that."<br /><br />NO. BUT HUMANS CAN. IT HAS BEEN DONE ONCE BEFORE.<br /><br />"No one would be that stu---"<br /><br />Susan stopped. Of course someone would be that stupid. Some humans would do anything to see if it was possible to do it. If you put a large switch in some cave somewhere, with a sign on it saying "End-of-the-World Switch. PLEASE DO NOT TOUCH," the paint wouldn't even have time to dry.</em><br /><br />- The monks' visit to Qu to see the "new toys" - exploding mandalas and prayer drum garottes.<br /><br />- Death's hilarious attempts to rally the other Horsemen for the Apocalypse. <br /><br />- Susan's unusual teaching techniques:<br /><br /><em>"What precisely was it you wanted, Madam?" she said. "It's only that I've left the class doing algebra, and they get restless when they've finished."<br /><br />"Algebra?" said Madam Frout, perforce staring at her own bosom, which no one else had ever done. "But that's far too difficult for seven-year-olds!"<br /><br />"Yes, but I didn't tell them that and so far they haven't found out," said Susan.</em><br /><br />- There was a raven named Quoth.<br /><br />That's one good thing about the Discworld series - even if you don't like the book as a whole, parts of it are sure to make you smile.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31688632" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1479520-novac" class="left imgcol" title="Novac"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1220231894p2/1479520.jpg" alt="Novac" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/31688632?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 31, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1479520-novac" class="user" title="Novac">Novac</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer31688632">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13277603856960157466">This was my first exposure to the work of Terry Pratchett. As a long-time Douglas Adams fan, I had heard Pratchett's name many times, but never took the time to actually read one of his books. I grabbed this one because the plot sounded interesting, and when I read the jacket at home, I noticed it was part of the "Discworld" series. Curious about how to properly start the series, a lump formed in my throat as I discovered that there are thirty-two Discworld novels, and that's not counting four y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13277603856960157466">This was my first exposure to the work of Terry Pratchett. As a long-time Douglas Adams fan, I had heard Pratchett's name many times, but never took the time to actually read one of his books. I grabbed this one because the plot sounded interesting, and when I read the jacket at home, I noticed it was part of the "Discworld" series. Curious about how to properly start the series, a lump formed in my throat as I discovered that there are thirty-two Discworld novels, and that's not counting four young adult novels, several graphic novels, multiple short stories, and a few science novels! In fact, there's even <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.lspace.org/books/reading-order-guides/the-discworld-reading-order-guide-1-5.jpg">a flowchart displaying the proper reading order for eight different sub-plots within the Discworld series</a>! Though this book is near the end of a reading order, I noticed that it was only "loosely" connected to the other books, so I went ahead and started reading. I could tell that I'd be reading more Pratchett (and more Discworld) books in the future shortly after I started. The Discworld is a mythology very similar to what you find in Lord of the Rings and Chronicles of Narnia, but much more irreverent. A very fun read — so much so that I decided to start at the beginning of this sub-plot reading order ("Death Novels") and read more Pratchett.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13277603856960157466">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_9994263">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9994263" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/112548-katherine-furman" class="left imgcol" title="Katherine Furman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442897797p2/112548.jpg" alt="Katherine Furman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/9994263?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 13, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/112548-katherine-furman" class="user" title="Katherine Furman">Katherine Furman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/112548-katherine-furman?shelf=fantasyscifi" class="actionLinkLite">fantasyscifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9994263">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7086070702581471591">A small disclaimer for this review: I read this book mostly while I had a fever, so I can't be held accountable for accuracy.<br /><br />This is the second Pratchett book I've read and though I enjoy him, it's hard for me to shake the thought that I'm reading Douglas Adams light, set in a Dungeons and Dragons fantasy land instead of sci-fi outer space. That's not altogether a bad thing though b/c I Adams is one of my very favorite authors and he did not leave this world with too many books. <br /><br /><em>Thief of Time</em>, a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7086070702581471591">A small disclaimer for this review: I read this book mostly while I had a fever, so I can't be held accountable for accuracy.<br /><br />This is the second Pratchett book I've read and though I enjoy him, it's hard for me to shake the thought that I'm reading Douglas Adams light, set in a Dungeons and Dragons fantasy land instead of sci-fi outer space. That's not altogether a bad thing though b/c I Adams is one of my very favorite authors and he did not leave this world with too many books. <br /><br /><em>Thief of Time</em>, appropriately, had some really interesting observations on the nature of time. How we spend it, waste it, kill it, etc. These observations made the book for me. It is generally funny, the characters enjoyable and quirky enough, but it's kind of run of the mill stuff you've seen before. But the peppering of genius dissections made it rise above. It was one of those books you just tear through, sucking down the story, but then out of nowhere you're struck by this quick, sentence-long kernel of knowledge that he nonchalantly threw in there and you're stopped dead in your tracks. You read it 5 times over, marveling at it's ingenuity and simplicity. And that's what I liked best about this book and in general what I love most about reading. I live for those simple little observational nuggets. Those things that the author, for the first time ever, took to a new level or in a new direction, that no one has ever taken it before. Somewhere that makes perfect, elegant sense. Written in a way that no one had ever been able to distill down it quite so purely before. You know, that kind of boiled down perfection that I'm not achieving in anyway in this review. Unfortunately towards the end of this book, Pratchett gets a little caught up in the mystical mood and forgets he's writing a comedy, but the fact that he can distill at all makes him worth reading. And it doesn't hurt that there's a grim reaper rat.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7086070702581471591">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10317891868908036500">Excellent book. It's up there in my top 5 Discworld books. Lu-Tze is my second favorite character, after Sam Vimes. I first encountered him in "Night Watch", and I wasn't so sure he wasn't just a stereotypical characterization of a crazyish monk.. I should've known better, having read several of Pratchett's books by then. It's a very interesting plot that makes you laugh, smirk, and think along the way. As usual, the pacing of the story is excellent. There's no real lag, and though there are sev</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10317891868908036500">Excellent book. It's up there in my top 5 Discworld books. Lu-Tze is my second favorite character, after Sam Vimes. I first encountered him in "Night Watch", and I wasn't so sure he wasn't just a stereotypical characterization of a crazyish monk.. I should've known better, having read several of Pratchett's books by then. It's a very interesting plot that makes you laugh, smirk, and think along the way. As usual, the pacing of the story is excellent. There's no real lag, and though there are several storylines going at once it is not difficult to keep up. As with most other Discworld stories, each character that's introduced plays an important role.. even if it's someone you would normally consider background noise. The more I read of this series (and I started with "Going Postal", which is (I think) book 27 or 28 and have bounced around since then.. It's not very serial, obviously), the more I come to love it and this book is a great example of why.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer962271749">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4984340186777332582">3/26/2004<br /><br />I don't know why I didn't review this one before. Death is featured, but once again, more play is given to granddaughter Susan, who, in the ongoing move to Discworld modernity, is now an elementary school teacher. There is an impending apocalypse caused by the Auditors again. We also get a few new characters: one a very talented clockmaker, another a novice under Lo Tze the time monk. Marvelous fun along the way as Pratchett explores what time means to humans. Such fun. There's a yeti.<br /><br />I</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4984340186777332582">3/26/2004<br /><br />I don't know why I didn't review this one before. Death is featured, but once again, more play is given to granddaughter Susan, who, in the ongoing move to Discworld modernity, is now an elementary school teacher. There is an impending apocalypse caused by the Auditors again. We also get a few new characters: one a very talented clockmaker, another a novice under Lo Tze the time monk. Marvelous fun along the way as Pratchett explores what time means to humans. Such fun. There's a yeti.<br /><br />I should note that reading the Death novels in order has really made me love them. At the moment Susan is my favorite character, although that could change as I read the other sequences.<br /><br />Library copy.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/4091267-rebecca-huston" class="user" title="Rebecca Huston">Rebecca Huston</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4091267-rebecca-huston?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4091267-rebecca-huston?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4091267-rebecca-huston?shelf=discworld" class="actionLinkLite">discworld</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer569707431">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9068812881889320641">Usually, if a series has more than a dozen books in it, I don't keep up with it. Most of the time it is too unwieldy and just plain boring. The author either starts to repeat themselves with characters and situations or goes off into outlandish events that just are not believable. Not so with Terry Pratchett -- his inventiveness and biting humour keeps me coming back for more. This one, Pratchett looks at the nature and elements of time, and wraps it all up in a pretty shiny bow for his readers.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9068812881889320641">Usually, if a series has more than a dozen books in it, I don't keep up with it. Most of the time it is too unwieldy and just plain boring. The author either starts to repeat themselves with characters and situations or goes off into outlandish events that just are not believable. Not so with Terry Pratchett -- his inventiveness and biting humour keeps me coming back for more. This one, Pratchett looks at the nature and elements of time, and wraps it all up in a pretty shiny bow for his readers. Susan, and her grandfather, Death, are back in this one, and two very interesting monks from a distant monastery -- Lu-Tse and Lobsang. This time, the Discworld itself is in peril from the Auditors, who find that the universe would be much more tidy if humans and their ilk would stop cluttering up the place. What ensues is a peculiar sort of Apocalypse, and one that kept me sitting up late into the night. Five stars overall, and very much recommended. <br /><br />For the longer review, please go here:<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.epinions.com/review/thief_of_time_by_terry_pratchett_2009_e_book/content_647058787972" target="_blank">http://www.epinions.com/review/thief_...</a></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_621326296">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/621326296" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3907768-claudiu" class="left imgcol" title="Claudiu"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1277277594p2/3907768.jpg" alt="Claudiu" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/621326296?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3907768-claudiu" class="user" title="Claudiu">Claudiu</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/515619.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780552148405" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer621326296">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1298395289034985284">It's been perhaps a whole year since I've last read Terry Pratchett. After 20-something books, you need to take a short rest from a certain universe, if you want to get anything done with your reading schedule.<br />It's easy to fall into the Discworld series and never surface again, especially as at this later part of the series there seems to exist a creative high that permeates every page and every line.<br /><br />I've come to a point in reading this series in which it's hard to call favorites. I can call out</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1298395289034985284">It's been perhaps a whole year since I've last read Terry Pratchett. After 20-something books, you need to take a short rest from a certain universe, if you want to get anything done with your reading schedule.<br />It's easy to fall into the Discworld series and never surface again, especially as at this later part of the series there seems to exist a creative high that permeates every page and every line.<br /><br />I've come to a point in reading this series in which it's hard to call favorites. I can call out the stinkers easy enough (Sourcery, Equal Rites, Soul Music, Reaper Man) but favorites are hard. This particular novel, however, comes pretty close to the very best of the series and I say that with full conviction. <br /><br />You can find within all that you hold dear about Pratchett: his very self-assured characters, the continuous evolution of the Discworld - whoever doesn't read this chronologically is in possession of an ill-mind -, bits and observations on the nature of us, and the Death of Rats which remains my most cherished of all of Terry Pratchett's creations. <br />I loath to retell the events of a book because it seems like I may cheat someone out of enjoying it themselves, so I can only say that this is one of the most convoluted, and at the same time simplest, stories this author has yet to write up to this point. The nature of Discworld time becomes apparent and we are treated to a story that features some new elements of this ever surprising world, and some old, woven in there for good measurement. <br /><br />One can always speak volumes about a bad book but it's hard to say why a book is good. This one is good for a plethora of reasons, from Death's continuous evolution as a character, to the new insights into the Discworld mythology, to the great pacing and the strong morals within. It's a novel that you can enjoy on any level, with or without any serious strain on the old noggin. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1298395289034985284">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20972026">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20972026" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1116185-kristen" class="left imgcol" title="Kristen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1241138579p2/1116185.jpg" alt="Kristen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20972026?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1116185-kristen" class="user" title="Kristen">Kristen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1116185-kristen?shelf=comedy" class="actionLinkLite">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20972026">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2832353120398377777">I have been reading Pratchett's books in order and have now completed #26... I have to say that reading what has taken him a lifetime to write is actually a very interesting experiment in watching a writer grow at his craft. Early Discworld books are one joke after another, with the plot simply stringing together the insanity of the humor... but as time has passed, his style had become far more plot driven and far less interested in the humor. True this book is still amusing, but one would read</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2832353120398377777">I have been reading Pratchett's books in order and have now completed #26... I have to say that reading what has taken him a lifetime to write is actually a very interesting experiment in watching a writer grow at his craft. Early Discworld books are one joke after another, with the plot simply stringing together the insanity of the humor... but as time has passed, his style had become far more plot driven and far less interested in the humor. True this book is still amusing, but one would read it for the plot versus the gags. I don't recall laughing out loud a single time while reading, though I did find much of the History Monks bits to be quite entertaining.<br /><br />Though they claim this is on of the "DEATH" books, Death plays a very small part, taking a backseat to his granddaughter Susan. Susan has moved on from being a nanny and is now a school mistress. Once again the Death of Rats shows up to tell her that her grandfather needs her to save humanity again. Susan has quite a knack for saving humanity.<br /><br />Then we have Jeremy, the clock maker... he has been employed by a mysterious woman to build a clock entirely out of glass that will tick with the beat of the world. She of course fails to tell him that a clock like this has been made before... and time stopped...<br /><br />Susan isn't the only one who will be out to stop Jeremy... we have Lu-Tse and his apprentice Lopsang who are sweepers at the dojo of the History Monks. The wisdom passed from Master to Apprentice is where you will find most of the humor in this book.<br /><br />The five horsemen of the apocalypse show up... yeah, turns out there were five but one quit a long time ago... but now worries... when it's time to ride out they'll all show up right? I mean Famine, War, Pestilence and Death are always ready to ride out right? Are you sure? Perhaps their hobbies have become more interesting to them.<br /><br />Then we have the bad guys... the Auditors, we all know them and despise them since they tried to take away Christmas, I mean Hogswatch. The auditors audit the Discworld and truly despise humanity because we are not orderly, tidy or easily cataloged. The auditors play a much larger role in this book than in any of Pratchett's previous works.<br /><br />Though I enjoyed reading this book, it won't go down as one of my favorite Discworld novels. The introduction of the History monks was nice, and I love Susan as a character... but on the whole the humor was more subtle than I would have liked, and the plot really didn't grab me the way some of the other plot driven novels did. Though Death and Susan are among my favorite characters, they always end up in my least favorite books. Amazing how that happens. Still I would suggest reading this book, it has a wonderful take on logic, rules, and time in general.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2832353120398377777">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5537530207769089056">Brillante a ratos como solo Sir Terry sabe ser. El último libro de la saga de la Muerte (por ahora) deja el protagonismo a su nieta Susan Sto-Helit, que junto con el barredor Lu-Tze acapara las líneas más memorables del libro.<br /><br />Tres estrellas porque es lo que merece cualquier cosa que escriba Pratchett, que da ese tono tan genial hasta a la lista de la compra.         <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1380735786">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14138569020733684236">Üheksa kümnendikku universumi massist on seletamata, sest see tegeleb ülejäänud universumi seletamisega - ja iseenda kukalt pole ju võimalik näha (välja arvatud väga väikestes universumites).<br /><br />Poe uksekell kõlises. Jeremy ohkas ja pani kellassepamonokli lauale. Kuid ta ei kiirustanud. Tema poes oli palju vaadata. Vahel pidi ta lausa köhatama, et kliendi tähelepanu äratada. Kui see juba jutuks tuli, siis pidi Jeremy vahel köhatama isegi selleks, et äratada iseenda peegelpildi tähelepanu, kui ta hab</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14138569020733684236">Üheksa kümnendikku universumi massist on seletamata, sest see tegeleb ülejäänud universumi seletamisega - ja iseenda kukalt pole ju võimalik näha (välja arvatud väga väikestes universumites).<br /><br />Poe uksekell kõlises. Jeremy ohkas ja pani kellassepamonokli lauale. Kuid ta ei kiirustanud. Tema poes oli palju vaadata. Vahel pidi ta lausa köhatama, et kliendi tähelepanu äratada. Kui see juba jutuks tuli, siis pidi Jeremy vahel köhatama isegi selleks, et äratada iseenda peegelpildi tähelepanu, kui ta habet ajas.<br /><br />Surm astus kaetud laua juurde ja haaras laudlina nurgast.<br />AEG ON LAUDLINA, lausus ta. SÖÖGIRIISTAD JA TALDRIKUD ON SÜNDMUSED, MIS AJAS ASET LEIAVAD...<br />Kostis trummipõrin. Susan vaatas põrandale - Rottide Surm istus tillukese trummikomplekti taga.<br /><br />Üks Igori endistest isandatest oli aga üleskeeratava mehikese tõepoolest v a l m i s teinud - puha kangid ja hoovad ja hammasrattad ja vedrud. Aju asemel oli sellel pikk lint, mille sisse olid löödud augud. Südame asemel oli tal suur vedru. Kui köögis oli kõik väga täpselt õigele kohale pandud, suutis see imeasi põrandat pühkida ja tassitäie talutavat teed valmistada. Kui aga kõik ei o l n u d väga täpselt õigele kohale pandud või sattus see tiksuv ja kõlksuv aparaat mõne ootamatu takistuse otsa, siis kiskus ta seintelt krohvi maha ja valmistas tassitäie maruvihast kassi.<br /><br />See avaldas Lu-Tzele muljet ja nii vanamees ka ütles. "Muljetavaldav," kiitis ta.<br /><br />Võõras vaikis. Võib-olla oli põhjuseks see, et tema nina ja suud kattis paks riie. Käsi varjasid rasked kindad. Ja see oli kummaline, sest tema ülejäänud keha kattis litritega õhtukleit. Ja naaritsakrae. Ja tal oli seljas seljakott. Ja peas tohutu suur vanaaegne naistekübar, millel oli piisavalt sulgi, et kolm haruldast liiki täiesti välja suretada.<br /><br />Lu-Tze uuris kõnelejat. Naine nägi välja nagu seltskonnadaam, kellel on seljataga väga karm päev rehepeksumasinas.<br /><br />Ta oli sunnitud vait jääma, sest ingel oli oma pea kohalt pühapaiste lahti kangutanud ja tõmbas sellega mööda lehtede kokkuroostetanud serva, nii et sädemeid lendas ja kostis heli, nagu libiseks kass mööda klassitahvlit alla.<br /><br />Kui nad Lu-Tze leidsid, vaatas see rahulikult otsa hiiglasuurele mammutile. Loom kissitas silmi oma tohutu lauba all, üritades vanameest vaadata ja samal ajal kõik oma kolm ajurakku üheskoos tööle panna, et otsustada, kas ta surnuks trampida või võhkadega härmatanud maastikust välja puskida. Üks ajurakk ütles "pusi", teine ütles "trambi", aga kolmas oli teemast kõrvale kaldunud ja mõtles seksist, nii palju kui võimalik.<br /><br />"Ma mõtlesin seda, et vahel, kui sa vaatad universumit ja mõtled: "Aga mina?", siis võib peaaegu kuulda universumit vastamas: "Mis siis sinust?""</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1182444495">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1182444495" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/861629-k" class="left imgcol" title="K."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1342794238p2/861629.jpg" alt="K." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1182444495?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/861629-k" class="user" title="K.">K.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/861629-k?shelf=fairy-tale-and-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fairy-tale-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/861629-k?shelf=smart-humor" class="actionLinkLite">smart-humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1182444495">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3553242769388704340">Not my usual fare, but after reading "The Wee Free Men" I willingly delved. "Wee Free Men" is more YA situated, whilst most of the rest of the Discworld series is directed at adults (or so I've read). Why? Perhaps just because the two "adult" Pratchetts I've read have been somewhat dizzying and many of the young set might not give it proper attention? Dunno. Anyway, there was nothing, NOTHING in this book unsuitable for a child to read in terms of violence, sex, language etc. Yes, a few swear wo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3553242769388704340">Not my usual fare, but after reading "The Wee Free Men" I willingly delved. "Wee Free Men" is more YA situated, whilst most of the rest of the Discworld series is directed at adults (or so I've read). Why? Perhaps just because the two "adult" Pratchetts I've read have been somewhat dizzying and many of the young set might not give it proper attention? Dunno. Anyway, there was nothing, NOTHING in this book unsuitable for a child to read in terms of violence, sex, language etc. Yes, a few swear words, but the kind I, who do not use even the mildest of them, laugh at instead of taking offense. <br /><br />I read that some of Pratchett's influences are Shakespeare, Tolkien, Wodehouse and Lovecraft. I haven't read Lovecraft, but you can see all of the other influences mixed in in a rather thrilling way. <br /><br />Despite being momentarily stunned by bizarrity (I know that's not a word, but here it fits) of the book at the beginning, there were several reasons I enjoyed this book tremendously.<br /><br />1) Death. Love him. Love his companions Death of Rats and Quoth the Raven. <br /><br />2) Susan, granddaughter of Death. Love her, she's wicked awesome (as in really, really cool, not wicked as in evil). <br /><br />3) Lady LeJean/Unity. Really, her journey is quite marvelous and thought-provoking. <br /><br />4) The many uses of chocolate, including one I didn't know about: its ability to destroy aliens. Well done!<br /><br />I've read that Pratchett employs some religious satire in his works (amongst other satire) and instead of finding this disturbing as a devout Christian, I rather found his ideas refreshing and thought-provoking. This book really had some stand-out moments in that regard. <br /><br />Super fun. Laugh out loud moments, which are always appreciated. <br /><br />Recommended to people who need to step outside this world for a few moments. Discworld is rather unlike. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3553242769388704340">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1398698941">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12177402618186767102">A solid 3.5. This is the first Pratchett book I can remember properly reading, so a fairly late introduction to his work. A friend lent me Thief of Time, so I picked it up and gave it a whirl.<br /><br />This was essentially my first foray into Discworld, so I'm sure plenty of plot nuance was lost on me. Lu-Tze was hilarious and someone I greatly enjoyed reading about, but all of the characters were notably vivid and well-drawn. The story rattled along nicely, and Pratchett even manages to make explanations</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12177402618186767102">A solid 3.5. This is the first Pratchett book I can remember properly reading, so a fairly late introduction to his work. A friend lent me Thief of Time, so I picked it up and gave it a whirl.<br /><br />This was essentially my first foray into Discworld, so I'm sure plenty of plot nuance was lost on me. Lu-Tze was hilarious and someone I greatly enjoyed reading about, but all of the characters were notably vivid and well-drawn. The story rattled along nicely, and Pratchett even manages to make explanations relating to time somewhat bearable! Amusingly enough, I completely forgot what Rule One was after starting the book, and so was utterly nonplussed whenever Lu-Tze or someone else frequently referred to it!<br /><br />There was quite a lot of wordplay that I enjoyed - and undoubtedly plenty more that I missed - throughout, and plenty of brilliant throwaway lines that had me laughing. Probable favourite was Pestilence, War and Famine being described as 'Sniffles, Scuffles and Localised Crop Failure' - excellent.<br /><br />On the whole it's a difficult book to judge without comparing it directly to others in the Discworld, but I did enjoy it. Nothing too groundbreaking and perhaps a tad too whimsical in the dialogue at points, but it was keenly observed and in a strange way, reflects real life oddly well. Mr. Pratchett was very clearly a British man!<br /><br />Not as funny or fantastic as Adams to my mind, but still thoroughly enjoyable. More please!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12177402618186767102">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer679337136">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2061594162066798758">I remember reading the book for the first time in 2007. I didn't like it and simply put it aside. Some time passed and I, being a huge Terry Pratchett fan, was literally running out of Discworld books (note I reread most of them several times). Somehow I started bumping into Thief of Time quotes on the net and somehow I got this feeling that maybe the time had come for me to give the book a second try. And I did. You know, the first thing I understood after a few pages was that you may be wrong.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2061594162066798758">I remember reading the book for the first time in 2007. I didn't like it and simply put it aside. Some time passed and I, being a huge Terry Pratchett fan, was literally running out of Discworld books (note I reread most of them several times). Somehow I started bumping into Thief of Time quotes on the net and somehow I got this feeling that maybe the time had come for me to give the book a second try. And I did. You know, the first thing I understood after a few pages was that you may be wrong. The thing I understood after turning the last one is that you may be definitely wrong and some books are just waiting for the right time, for the right, wiser you to be understood. And this is one of such books. It's incredibly funny, extremely inventive and infinitely wise. I just didn't get what it was about because I wasn't ready to appreciate it, no author's fault. But now I do. Because it is such an amazing book, so clever and so wise I literally stopped reading to taste the ideas in my mind. Thank you, Sir Terry Pratchett again. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2061594162066798758">...more</a>

        <a href="/review/show/143671437?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2564574-autumn" class="user" title="Autumn">Autumn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/48002.Thief_of_Time" title="Paperback 9780061031328" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2564574-autumn?shelf=a-world-of-their-own" class="actionLinkLite">a-world-of-their-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2564574-autumn?shelf=laughter" class="actionLinkLite">laughter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143671437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9831070941759373793">As always, Pratchett is fantastic. Want good, smart, "you're as smart as I am so hop in" humor? Read Pratchett. It's like being in on the joke even if you've never heard it before; Pratchett knows you'll get it anyway and appreciate it. <br /><br />Wonderful, as always, to have Susan in the story. I think we should follow her education methods more often. Death is always entertaining to have around, especially thinking about him drinking tea from a mug labeled, "World's Greatest Granddad" and actually havin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9831070941759373793">As always, Pratchett is fantastic. Want good, smart, "you're as smart as I am so hop in" humor? Read Pratchett. It's like being in on the joke even if you've never heard it before; Pratchett knows you'll get it anyway and appreciate it. <br /><br />Wonderful, as always, to have Susan in the story. I think we should follow her education methods more often. Death is always entertaining to have around, especially thinking about him drinking tea from a mug labeled, "World's Greatest Granddad" and actually having to convince the rest of his Horsemen to ride out for the Apocalypse. And Igor reminds me so much of an oddly shaped Jeeves that I had to laugh every time he appeared. Who else is suave enough to respond to their employer's insistence that they're not insane because they "have a paper saying so," with a simple, "Well done, sir." ? Wonderful.<br /><br />Pratchett masterfully handles a topic that anyone else would have bumbled with. Stopping time with a big glass clock; rotating wooden scrolls that somehow record time and keep it going; death by chocolate (oh, yes, real poof, you're gone death). Wonderful stuff.<br /><br />And did I mention I think Susan should be in charge of education?<br /><br />Also, always remember Rule Number One.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer137261717">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer889109062779694933">Comment fait <a title="Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry pratchett</a> ? A chaque tome, je me demande si il pourra encore explorer de nouveaux aspects de son monde à tiroir, et à chaque tome, il le fait spectaculairement. Dans ce tome, il s'attaque, dans le désordre, aux cavaliers de l'apocalypse, aux vieux moines pleins de sagesse, au temps qui passe, en passant par les musées inutiles. Et chacun de ces sujets mérite qu'on en parle, ce qui est malheureusement très difficile sans déflorer l'intrigue, habilement construite comme d'habitu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText889109062779694933">Comment fait <a title="Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry pratchett</a> ? A chaque tome, je me demande si il pourra encore explorer de nouveaux aspects de son monde à tiroir, et à chaque tome, il le fait spectaculairement. Dans ce tome, il s'attaque, dans le désordre, aux cavaliers de l'apocalypse, aux vieux moines pleins de sagesse, au temps qui passe, en passant par les musées inutiles. Et chacun de ces sujets mérite qu'on en parle, ce qui est malheureusement très difficile sans déflorer l'intrigue, habilement construite comme d'habitude.<br />Les cavaliers de l'apocalypse, donc, reprennent une cavalcade, ce qui est difficule pour ces représentations anthropomorphiques qui se sont habituées, semble-t-il, à leur humanité. Heureusement pour elles, le dernier n'est pas, je trouve, le moindre (je lui ai même trouvé une classe largement supérieure à la Pestilence, par exemple, ce qui n'a rien d'étonnant vu l'époque).<br />Suzanne Sto Hellit joue pleinement dans ce roman son rôle de voix de la raison froide, limite cynique, qui va quand même sauver tout le monde. En fait, elle a un rôle que je trouve bien plus marquant que dans <a title="Accros du roc" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Accros%20du%20roc">Accros du roc</a> ou <a title="le Père Porcher" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=le%20P%C3%A8re%20Porcher">le Père Porcher</a>, sans doute parce qu'elle y est définitivement plus adulte et consciente de sa place très particulière dans le Disque-Monde.<br />Il y a évidement un Igor qui se balade dans un coin, et qui ne manque pas de placer des répliques savoureuses dès qu'on lui laisse ouvrir la bouche.<br />Mais évidement, la gloire de ce roman, ce sont le balayeur et son apprenti. Des personnages qui montrent à quel point un vieux maître boudhisto-truc-bidule peut être, une fois muni de la dose suffisante d'humour et d'auto-dérision, absolument redoutable pour ceux qui l'entourent. Surtout que ce balayeur-ci est muni de la doctrine très particulière d'une demoiselle d'Ankh-Morpock ...<br />Bon, bien sûr, vous me direz que le Disque-Monde, je suis fan. C'est vrai.<br />Cela dit, j'ai trouvé à ce roman une saveur particulière. Peut-être à cause de ce moine boudhiste qui m'a légèrement rappelé celui du film avec Eddy Murphy : Gloden Child, l'enfant du Tibet. Parce que c'est pas tous les jours qu'on rencontre un bonze qui ne se prend clairement pas au sérieux, et qui préfère le balai à la baston. Peut-êtyre aussi que ce nouveau cavalier de l'apocalypse, parfaitement en phase avec notre époque, a réveillé un groupe tombant dans la routine. Peut-être enfin parce que les hommes en noir de ce récit sont parfaitement représentatifs de la bureaucratie. En tout cas, une chose est sûre, il rentre dans la liste des tous meilleurs tomes de cette série, longue, excellente, mais parfois plus excellente encore.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="889109062779694933">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3995768716803267882">Bueno, para empezar decir que se trata de Mundodisco y de Terry Pratchett con lo cual como mínimo tengo que decir que sigue siendo genial. Y en este además se genera algo grande dentro del mismo libro.<br /><br />Pero vayamos por partes, podemos empezar hablando del humor de Pratchett que se destila de cada una de las páginas, pero con eso no acabaríamos nunca porque es un humor que, o bien te deja indiferente o bien te enamora.         <a href="/review/show/116658335?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3167691-lindsey-duncan" class="user" title="Lindsey Duncan">Lindsey Duncan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3167691-lindsey-duncan?shelf=funny-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">funny-fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer116658335">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3695525857111254907">In my experience, there are two types of Pratchett novels: those that start with a tight focus on a single character / plotline and explode outwards, and those that start with several characters / plotlines and converge inwards. To me, the former are far superior, the latter never quite coming together. I never feel like the plot totally makes sense, the characters keep you at arm's length ... and it never quite feels as if they've earned the resolution.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Thief of Time is one of the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3695525857111254907">In my experience, there are two types of Pratchett novels: those that start with a tight focus on a single character / plotline and explode outwards, and those that start with several characters / plotlines and converge inwards. To me, the former are far superior, the latter never quite coming together. I never feel like the plot totally makes sense, the characters keep you at arm's length ... and it never quite feels as if they've earned the resolution.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Thief of Time is one of the latter. The narrative is clever and some of the Discworld's best characters make their appearances, but it's hard to engage with the story. There are some intriguing extensions from earlier books, but I'm not sure whether they would be quite as absorbing for someone who wasn't familiar with those elements.<br /><br />The exploration of humanity, the horsemen of the Apocalypse, the long-suffering Igor - and the mere presence of Susan Sto Helit - are worth reading the book on their own. Ultimately, however, I felt I was reading the book less for the throughline as for the "good bits." The sideshow was great. I was lukewarm on the main event.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15522240?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 15, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/154362-mirna" class="user" title="Mirna">Mirna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer15522240'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15522240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4004692898046265905">All hail Pratchett!! Ini adalah buku Pratchett kesembilan yang saya baca. HURRAH! <br /><br />Sesuai judulnya Pratchett kali ini memfokuskan kisah pada Waktu yang ternyata bentuk personifikasinya adalah perempuan, yang jatuh cinta pada seorang pendiri aliran kepercayaan bahwa waktu dapat dipahami bernama Wen the Eternally Surprised, yang belakangan pengikutnya disebut Historian Monks. Bukan biksu sejarawan, tapi Biksu Pengatur Sejarah. Orang-orang Ordo Wen ini tinggal di lembah yang waktunya beku pada keada</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4004692898046265905">All hail Pratchett!! Ini adalah buku Pratchett kesembilan yang saya baca. HURRAH! <br /><br />Sesuai judulnya Pratchett kali ini memfokuskan kisah pada Waktu yang ternyata bentuk personifikasinya adalah perempuan, yang jatuh cinta pada seorang pendiri aliran kepercayaan bahwa waktu dapat dipahami bernama Wen the Eternally Surprised, yang belakangan pengikutnya disebut Historian Monks. Bukan biksu sejarawan, tapi Biksu Pengatur Sejarah. Orang-orang Ordo Wen ini tinggal di lembah yang waktunya beku pada keadaan selalu sempurna bagaikan musim semi, literally. Dan di kuil mereka yang rahasia itu terdapat alat pengatur waktu raksasa yang mampu mengambil dan membuang waktu sesuka hati, biksu-biksunya belajar mengiris waktu yang artinya mereka bisa bergerak sangat cepat dengan manipulasi waktu, terdapat sebuah taman berisi lima kejutan yang diisi deretan bonsai gunung, dan seorang master rahasia bernama Lu Tze atau dikenal oleh siswanya sebagai The Sweeper yang dalam kesehariannya adalah...seorang tukang sapu.<br /><br />Waktu punya dua skandal. Yang pertama adalah hubungan cintanya yang menghasilkan anak lelaki. Lalu yang terakhir adalah peristiwa dikurungnya Waktu dalam sebuah jam dari kaca. Yang terakhir inilah isyu utama Thief of Time karena dikurungnya waktu artinya kiamat, dan seseorang atau sesuatu sedang membangun ulang jam kaca itu.<br /><br />Death tentu saja harus terlibat karena kiamat itu kejadian besar. Kiamat atau Apocalypse membutuhkan 4 penunggang kuda jaman kiamat alias the 4 Apocalypse horse rider. War, Famine, Pestilence, dan Death. Selain Death, ketiga rekannya ini terpengaruh perkembangan jaman modern sehingga mereka menjadi “kurang sakti” lagi. Bagaikan the Beatles ternyata ada anggota ke lima yang keluar sebelum The Riders ini ngetop. Yaitu Kaos. Kaos kurang “menjual” sehingga ia berhenti, lalu berubah profesi menjadi tukang susu yang terpercaya, dan non-chaotic alias sangat teratur. Pada saat “kiamat” akhirnya kelima tokoh antropomorphic ini bergabung dalam pertemuan reuni dan menghancurkan musuh bersama yaitu para Auditors yang dalam bentuk manusia akan langsung tewas begitu kena coklat. Something had to do with the hormonal orgasmic experience. Oh yeaahhh! Now I know why I LOVE chocolate!<br /><br />Tokoh utama kali ini adalah Jeremy si tukang jam, dan Lobsang Ludd, biksu muda mantan maling yang punya bakat alamiah memanipulasi waktu. Dipandu Lu Tze dengan kitab berisi kata-kata bijak yang didapatnya dari seorang perempuan tua mantan induk semangnya di Ankh-Morpork, Nyonya Kosmopilite, Lobsang Ludd berusaha memecahkan misteri asal-usulnya. Death di lain pihak, karena merasa terganggu dengan kiamat sebelum waktunya ini, mengirimkan bala bantuan berupa Susan Sto Helit, yang sedang kesal pada kakeknya dan the Death of Rats. <br />Di akhir cerita semua orang bahagia termasuk cucu perempuan Death yang menemukan teman bermain yang akan lebih memahami dunianya, yaitu anak lelaki Time.<br /><br />Banyak kata-kata bijak yang dapat dicuplik dari buku ini. Pratchett menunjukkan kalau Nenek bilang itu berbahaya, Nenek pasti benar.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4004692898046265905">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer740403309232915953">My MOST FAVORITE of all the Discworld series. Many awesome things are in the book. Death disappears and finds out that the "five" riders of the apocalypse have become lazy drunkards, reminiscing on the good old days. His granddaughter, Susan (one of my favorite characters) is a school teacher who can manipulate time and reality, and has the power of suggestion. She goes in search of her grandfather, and stumbles onto a plot by the auditors of reality to end the universe. They are trying to convi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText740403309232915953">My MOST FAVORITE of all the Discworld series. Many awesome things are in the book. Death disappears and finds out that the "five" riders of the apocalypse have become lazy drunkards, reminiscing on the good old days. His granddaughter, Susan (one of my favorite characters) is a school teacher who can manipulate time and reality, and has the power of suggestion. She goes in search of her grandfather, and stumbles onto a plot by the auditors of reality to end the universe. They are trying to convice the worlds best clockmaker to make the ultimate and most accurate clock, which, when operational, will stop time forever. The monks of time find out about this and sent Lu Tze the sweeper (and also time master of Deja Fu martial arts) and his assistant to stop this from happening. Actually, the monks don't send him, he sneaks around them. Anyways, read the book, because such funny concepts are introduced, and the book is really quite enjoyable.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_196191097">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196191097" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="left imgcol" title="Wastrel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1317660831p2/5743748.jpg" alt="Wastrel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/196191097?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="user" title="Wastrel">Wastrel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/338723.Thief_of_Time" title="Hardcover 9780385601887" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=r-ss" class="actionLinkLite">r-ss</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=z-2001" class="actionLinkLite">z-2001</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=fantastika-bildungsroman" class="actionLinkLite">fantastika-bildungsroman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer196191097">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9074618650108835770">A frustrating installment - Pratchett at his very best, at the service of plot, themes and characters that aren't really in the upper echelon. The result is entertaining for at least two thirds of the book, but rather unravels once the finale starts pulling on its threads. The ending doesn't just not fully work, its flaccidity deflates the rest of the book. I was really enjoying reading this... but when I finished, I felt disappointed and underwhelmed.<br /><br />That said, it's much better than I remember</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9074618650108835770">A frustrating installment - Pratchett at his very best, at the service of plot, themes and characters that aren't really in the upper echelon. The result is entertaining for at least two thirds of the book, but rather unravels once the finale starts pulling on its threads. The ending doesn't just not fully work, its flaccidity deflates the rest of the book. I was really enjoying reading this... but when I finished, I felt disappointed and underwhelmed.<br /><br />That said, it's much better than I remember it being. It has some good jokes, some really great ruminations, and some highly effective dramatic scenes. It's a long way above Pratchett's worst... the problem is, given the talent and mastery he shows in places here, it ought to be closer to his best...<br /><br />For my full review, <a rel="nofollow" href="https://vacuouswastrel.wordpress.com/2015/05/14/thief-of-time-by-terry-pratchett/">check out my blog.</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9074618650108835770">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10099488460120657915">I appreciated some parodies like the reservoir dogs or the gadget geek from 007 series, I also had a feeling of familiarity with Good Omens, although something was off, for the last quarter of the book I just wanted it to end. The Susan character felt a bit forced at the end, Death and related characters around been underused. And those crazy accountants were so exasperating!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer814347630">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13501648971985476000">I've never been a big Pratchett fan, I think partly because I always thought he wrote the tales of redwall, which of course he didn't. When my Sister handed me this to read I was a bit pensive, but she said it was funny, and I had a Christmas break on my hands so I gave it a go. <br /><br />I am very glad I did. <br /><br />The wit and wisdom in these discworld novels (I have now read 2) seems to get better and better as they go on. There is a type of wry, cynical depression behind them (characterized by death, offish</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13501648971985476000">I've never been a big Pratchett fan, I think partly because I always thought he wrote the tales of redwall, which of course he didn't. When my Sister handed me this to read I was a bit pensive, but she said it was funny, and I had a Christmas break on my hands so I gave it a go. <br /><br />I am very glad I did. <br /><br />The wit and wisdom in these discworld novels (I have now read 2) seems to get better and better as they go on. There is a type of wry, cynical depression behind them (characterized by death, offish monks and unknowing smart-asses in this particular book) that is entrancing and somehow (bizarrely) uplifting. <br /><br />Go into this with your eyes open. Nothing makes any sense, which, for a control freak like me is ideal. The characters are unbelievable, the storyline entirely misunderstandable, and that my friends is the joy of it!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13501648971985476000">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And history monks. <br /><br />Thank you for all you have written, Sir Terry.</span>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gnDWJVXGDr9rfDUgR7i7Icvhg8YM0rFg4D2nJrurQCDnpOn2pxQaReekQZs52V2TghZA30UP9sqKNKK0dz62ZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6fZAG6zo3mr3Fj/qbhrviGVY94CVuHE8CvannQuYe06MIn/IXjrKkHvOS1EQewk6LK80mdxlNpZg/6IPxw2NCw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><img alt="1654" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p2/1654.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14957107905697150770">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14957107905697150770">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <em>The Color of Magic</em>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <em>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</em>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <em>Good Omens</em>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <em>Nation</em>. Terry published <em>Snuff</em> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14957107905697150770">...more</a>

    </div>
